# Consultation 68 — External DX review from a real plugin author

After Phase 4 landed (commits `09c377a` docs + `f5858ce` triad
archive), the user handed `docs/integration-guide.md` to a separate
Claude instance ("lottery-claude") that is building a real test
plugin in another project. That instance came back with a tight,
specific DX critique. The user wants the triad to validate the
findings, prescribe fixes, and decide what's in scope for a
Phase 4.1 DX polish commit vs what belongs on the roadmap.

This is the first external review the V1 surface has received.
Treat it as authoritative on developer experience — the issues are
things a plugin author actually hit, not a static-review nitpick.

## Verbatim external review

> ### What's solid
>
> - `docs/crypto-spec.md` — rigorous and complete. AAD shapes,
>   envelope canonical bytes, KDF flow, Python reference snippets,
>   even live-card AAD. Nothing to fix here.
> - Server endpoint surface — no "secret" endpoints; everything
>   maps cleanly to the integration guide's workflow. No
>   undocumented escape hatches.
> - Manifest validation source-of-truth
>   (`sdk-plugin/src/manifest.ts:111-204`) — strictly enforces the
>   renderer ↔ template ↔ cardType ↔ cardKeyPath matrix the guide
>   claims. The guide isn't lying.
>
> ### What needs work (priority order)
>
> **1. The bundleHash/signature footgun is unowned.**
> `manifest.ts:127` only checks "is this a hex string." `"00"`
> passes. The server only catches it at publish time with a 422.
> Your own SDK README (line 34) tells authors to write
> `bundleHash: '00'` with no "for development only" annotation. We
> hit this and chased the wrong cause for ages. Fix: either (a)
> make the SDK validator require 64/128 hex chars, or (b) document
> the `"00"` means I haven't signed yet pattern explicitly.
>
> **2. Pairing is half-built and the docs admit it.**
> `sdk-python/README.md:29-37` has a comment "(M7 wires this; for
> now in dev, use `client.set_pairing(...)`)" — this reads like a
> TODO leaking into shipped docs. The integration guide §8 fills
> the gap with manual "copy `user_id` and `pairing_key_hex` from
> app UI, paste into Python" — fine for dogfood, bad for a
> first-impressions guide. The plugin SDK README doesn't cover
> pairing at all and the python SDK README is mid-refactor. Pick
> one canonical home for the pairing dance and finish it.
>
> **3. The wildcard rule is buried in code.**
> `sdk-plugin/src/network.ts:48-62` is the only canonical
> reference. The SDK README mentions "single path or host segment
> wildcard" in one line; the integration guide is silent. As I
> noted in my first pass: this cost us a session. One sentence in
> the guide near `declaredEndpoints` would prevent every author
> from hitting it.
>
> **4. No example plugin exists.**
> `examples/` has one directory (`trading-bot`) and its README
> literally says "This example doesn't ship a plugin; it just
> exercises the sender side." So the only place authors can see an
> actual `render()` function is the inline snippets in the
> integration guide. There's no `examples/minimal-plugin/`, no
> `npm create @syncler/plugin` scaffold, no copy-and-modify base.
> This is the single biggest "scale to 10 plugin authors" risk —
> every author starts from a blank canvas.
>
> **5. `platform.network.fetch` error contract is undocumented.**
> The integration guide §3 mentions it works. Nothing tells you
> what it throws on offline, what it returns on 5xx, or whether
> there's a timeout. Authors building offline-aware cards (like
> ours) have to discover this by trial and error. Document the
> contract.
>
> **6. ROADMAP.md is feature-focused, ignores DX.**
> The roadmap covers nonce-replay durability, multi-process plugin
> host, per-device encryption — all platform internals. None of
> the DX issues we hit (empty-hash footgun, no example plugin,
> half-built pairing, undocumented wildcard, no fetch error
> contract) appear anywhere on the roadmap. That's a signal the
> platform team isn't tracking developer-facing friction as work.
>
> ### One structural suggestion
>
> The integration guide is 11 sections of prose and the "Common
> errors" §9 is a flat list. As the surface grows you'll want a
> "Common pitfalls" section separate from server error codes —
> pitfalls is "things that pass validation but bite you later"
> (empty hash, single-segment wildcard, missing `registerPlugin`,
> `cardKeyPath` ↔ `card_key` mismatch), errors is "the server said
> no, here's what to do." Today they're conflated and that hides
> the real footguns.
>
> ### Bottom line
>
> Crypto and protocol are solid. The DX layer is roughly where we
> found it in our session: the platform works, but the on-ramp
> expects an author who'll read code when docs disagree. Fixing #1,
> #2, #3, and #4 would meaningfully change first-impression
> quality. #5 and #6 are smaller but cheap wins.

## What the triad needs to decide

For each finding (1–6 + structural):

1. **Validate the claim.** Cross-check against the actual code at
   HEAD (`f5858ce`). Cite file:line on both sides. Is the
   complaint factually correct, partially correct, or wrong?

2. **Classify the fix.** One of:
   - **Phase 4.1 (commit now)**: small doc/SDK-validator change,
     no architectural decision needed.
   - **Phase 4.5 (medium effort)**: needs design (e.g. scaffold
     command, example plugin), but doable as a follow-up commit
     in the V1 milestone before broader rollout.
   - **V1.5+ roadmap**: needs deferred design or platform work.

3. **Concrete prescription.** Specific files to change with line
   refs. For doc additions, suggest the exact section + 1–3
   sentence framing. For SDK changes, suggest the validator
   signature or scaffold command shape.

4. **Cross-finding interactions.** E.g. #4 (example plugin) and #3
   (wildcard documentation) probably want to land together so the
   example uses a wildcard endpoint and the docs explain why; #1
   (bundleHash footgun) likely needs both a validator change AND
   an example-plugin demonstration to be fully fixed.

## My read (for the triad to confirm or push back on)

The bullets I'd want to land in a Phase 4.1 DX polish commit:

- **#1**: validator-level fix in `manifest.ts` — require hex string
  length ∈ {64, 128} (32-byte SHA-256 = 64 hex; some bundle hashes
  may be 64-byte = 128 hex if anyone's using SHA-512). Plus a
  README annotation that the build tool (`sign-bundle.ts`) replaces
  the placeholder.
- **#3**: one paragraph in `docs/integration-guide.md §2` next to
  the `declaredEndpoints` reference + a code-comment in
  `sdk-plugin/src/network.ts` linking back to the guide section.
- **#5**: a new subsection in `docs/integration-guide.md §3` (or a
  new §3.1) documenting what `platform.network.fetch` throws and
  returns. Pull the actual error shapes from
  `android/.../capabilities/NetworkBridge.kt` and
  `sdk-plugin/src/runtime.ts`.
- **Structural**: rename §9 to "Common server errors" and add a
  new §9.1 "Common pitfalls" — empty hash footgun, single-segment
  wildcard, missing `registerPlugin()`, `cardKeyPath` ↔ `card_key`
  mismatch, host-renderer-only fields on template manifests.
- **#6**: add a "Developer experience" V1.5 section to ROADMAP.md
  listing #2 (pairing flow), #4 (example plugin + scaffold), and a
  named owner if the user wants one.

The bullets I'd want to defer:

- **#2 pairing dance**: lottery-claude is right it's half-built,
  but landing the canonical pairing flow needs UX work in the
  Android app (auto-issue a pairing-key copy screen post-confirm)
  AND server-side support for "did the user complete this token"
  polling. Document the current dogfood path more clearly and put
  the canonical flow on the V1.5 roadmap.
- **#4 example plugin**: agreed it's the highest-leverage thing
  for adoption, but writing a real `examples/minimal-plugin/` that
  actually round-trips needs ~half a day of work (write a tiny
  backend, sign a bundle, document the run loop). Roadmap it as
  V1.5 #16 (DX) and ship Phase 4.1 without it.

Triad: push back on this split if you disagree. Is anything I'm
deferring actually a 30-minute fix I'm overestimating?

   wrong), classify (4.1 / 4.5 / roadmap), prescribe.
2. Push back on my proposed split if you disagree.
3. Overall: ready to execute / specific blockers.

If both reviewers GREEN on the split, I'll execute Phase 4.1, fire
one more triad on the result, and ship.

The server reconstructs the envelope from the request fields and verifies against the registered sender's public key. docs\crypto-spec.md:276:**`user_id` is REQUIRED in the envelope.** Without it, a delete signature valid for one user's card could be replayed against another user's card with a coincidentally matching `(sender_id, card_key)` — the table is uniquely keyed on `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)`, so the lookup would otherwise be ambiguous. (Codex consultation 62 security finding.) The server matches the exact triple before deleting; mismatched triples no-op silently and still publish a `card.delete` SSE event so all of the user's devices clear any stale local copy.

docs\integration-guide.md:275:**JSONPath dialect.** Only `$.field(.subfield)*` is accepted. No array indexing (`$.items[0]`), no wildcards (`$.*`), no filters (`$.items[?(@.x>0)]`). Field-name segments must match `[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*`. The server rejects manifests with malformed paths at publish time, and the client-side resolver returns `null` for malformed input as a defense-in-depth.
docs\integration-guide.md:293:- Every `action.endpoint` matches at least one of your declared `endpoints` globs (the same glob syntax that gates `platform.network.fetch` in script renderers).
docs\integration-guide.md:298:Set `card_type="live"` to ship a persistent, upsertable card. The plugin manifest must also provide `card_key_path` — a JSONPath into your decrypted payload that yields the stable identity for each card (e.g. `$.order_id`). This lets the inbox merge multiple upserts for the same logical card into one row.
docs\integration-guide.md:306:    bundle_signature=bytes.fromhex(manifest["signature"]),

docs\integration-guide.md:367:    card_key="order-456",
docs\integration-guide.md:375:**`card_key` must equal `card_key_path` resolved on the plaintext.** The manifest's `card_key_path` (declared at publish time, e.g. `"$.order_id"`) is the path the host extracts on decrypt to use as the merge key for this card. The `card_key` you pass to `upsert_card` is what the server stores. If the two disagree, the host's per-card merge breaks and your "live" card behaves like a series of event cards. The server doesn't cross-check the two — enforcement is your responsibility. (V1 validates `card_key_path` only as `startswith("$")`; a future phase will tighten this to the full `$.field(.subfield)*` JSONPath grammar used by template fields.)
docs\integration-guide.md:385:- **Rate limit.** Fixed window of 60 upserts per minute per `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)`; else 429. (There's also an IP-bucketed pre-auth limit of 120/min for cheap DoS protection.)
docs\integration-guide.md:394:    card_key="order-456",
docs\integration-guide.md:398:`user_id` is **required**. The canonical signed envelope binds `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)` — without `user_id` in the signature, an attacker (or a coincidence: two users with the same `card_key` under the same sender) could be deleted by mistake. The delete endpoint matches exactly that triple in the row lookup.

docs\integration-guide.md:464:Note: the platform does **not** inject `device_id` into the body for you in V1. If you need to distinguish which device acted, include a sender-generated identifier in your payload and (for script renderer) have the plugin echo it back. docs\integration-guide.md:496:## 9. Common errors
docs\integration-guide.md:498:- **`401 invalid envelope signature`** — your sender's Ed25519 key doesn't match the one registered. Re-check `private_key_path`.
docs\integration-guide.md:507:- **`409 sequence_number not greater than existing`** (cards upsert) — the existing card has a `sequence_number` ≥ what you sent. Sequence must be strictly increasing per `card_key`.
docs\integration-guide.md:508:- **Card shows "render failed: plugin did not install __syncler_internal_dispatch — missing registerPlugin() call?"** — your bundle defined the plugin class but didn't call `registerPlugin(new YourPlugin())` at module scope. See §3.
docs\integration-guide.md:509:- **Card shows "endpoint not declared"** — your `onclick` handler is calling a URL that doesn't match any pattern in your manifest's `declaredEndpoints`. Add the URL pattern (globs allowed: `https://example.com/api/*`) and re-publish.

docs\crypto-spec.md:150:### Message Envelope (Ed25519 sender signature input)
docs\crypto-spec.md:156:The sender signs the canonical envelope JSON with Ed25519. The server reconstructs the envelope from the request fields and verifies against the registered sender's public key. Envelope is also what the recipient device uses to verify the signature on inbox fetch — therefore inbox/detail responses include `expires_at` (in addition to the body, nonce, signature).

docs\crypto-spec.md:222:Live cards are persistent, upsertable units identified by `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)`. The encrypted payload uses the same AES-256-GCM primitive as messages, but with a richer AAD that binds the card-specific metadata. Upsert and delete each have their own Ed25519 envelope distinct from the message envelope.

docs\crypto-spec.md:276:**`user_id` is REQUIRED in the envelope.** Without it, a delete signature valid for one user's card could be replayed against another user's card with a coincidentally matching `(sender_id, card_key)` — the table is uniquely keyed on `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)`, so the lookup would otherwise be ambiguous. (Codex consultation 62 security finding.) The server matches the exact triple before deleting; mismatched triples no-op silently and still publish a `card.delete` SSE event so all of the user's devices clear any stale local copy.

docs\integration-guide.md:275:**JSONPath dialect.** Only `$.field(.subfield)*` is accepted. No array indexing (`$.items[0]`), no wildcards (`$.*`), no filters (`$.items[?(@.x>0)]`). Field-name segments must match `[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*`. The server rejects manifests with malformed paths at publish time, and the client-side resolver returns `null` for malformed input as a defense-in-depth.
docs\integration-guide.md:293:- Every `action.endpoint` matches at least one of your declared `endpoints` globs (the same glob syntax that gates `platform.network.fetch` in script renderers).
docs\integration-guide.md:298:Set `card_type="live"` to ship a persistent, upsertable card. The plugin manifest must also provide `card_key_path` — a JSONPath into your decrypted payload that yields the stable identity for each card (e.g. `$.order_id`). This lets the inbox merge multiple upserts for the same logical card into one row.
docs\integration-guide.md:306:    bundle_signature=bytes.fromhex(manifest["signature"]),

docs\integration-guide.md:349:    card_key="order-456",
docs\integration-guide.md:367:    card_key="order-456",
docs\integration-guide.md:375:**`card_key` must equal `card_key_path` resolved on the plaintext.** The manifest's `card_key_path` (declared at publish time, e.g. `"$.order_id"`) is the path the host extracts on decrypt to use as the merge key for this card. The `card_key` you pass to `upsert_card` is what the server stores. If the two disagree, the host's per-card merge breaks and your "live" card behaves like a series of event cards. The server doesn't cross-check the two — enforcement is your responsibility. (V1 validates `card_key_path` only as `startswith("$")`; a future phase will tighten this to the full `$.field(.subfield)*` JSONPath grammar used by template fields.)
docs\integration-guide.md:385:- **Rate limit.** Fixed window of 60 upserts per minute per `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)`; else 429. (There's also an IP-bucketed pre-auth limit of 120/min for cheap DoS protection.)
docs\integration-guide.md:394:    card_key="order-456",
docs\integration-guide.md:398:`user_id` is **required**. The canonical signed envelope binds `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)` — without `user_id` in the signature, an attacker (or a coincidence: two users with the same `card_key` under the same sender) could be deleted by mistake. The delete endpoint matches exactly that triple in the row lookup.

docs\integration-guide.md:464:Note: the platform does **not** inject `device_id` into the body for you in V1. docs\integration-guide.md:496:## 9. Common errors
docs\integration-guide.md:498:- **`401 invalid envelope signature`** — your sender's Ed25519 key doesn't match the one registered. Re-check `private_key_path`.
docs\integration-guide.md:507:- **`409 sequence_number not greater than existing`** (cards upsert) — the existing card has a `sequence_number` ≥ what you sent. Sequence must be strictly increasing per `card_key`.
docs\integration-guide.md:508:- **Card shows "render failed: plugin did not install __syncler_internal_dispatch — missing registerPlugin() call?"** — your bundle defined the plugin class but didn't call `registerPlugin(new YourPlugin())` at module scope. See §3.
docs\integration-guide.md:509:- **Card shows "endpoint not declared"** — your `onclick` handler is calling a URL that doesn't match any pattern in your manifest's `declaredEndpoints`. Add the URL pattern (globs allowed: `https://example.com/api/*`) and re-publish.

  32:     suspend fun fetch(plugin: PluginInstance, argsJson: String): String = withContext(Dispatchers.IO) {
  33:         val args = JsonBridgeCodec.objectFrom(argsJson)
  34:         val url = args["url"] as? String ?: return@withContext JsonBridgeCodec.error("invalid_args")
  35:         // Bridge-level scheme check: defense in depth against an injected
  36:         // OkHttpClient whose connectionSpecs might not align with this
  37:         // bridge's release-HTTPS policy. Enforcing scheme here means we
  38:         // fail closed regardless of how `client` was built.
  39:         val schemeOk = url.startsWith("https://") || (BuildConfig.DEBUG && url.startsWith("http://"))
  40:         if (!schemeOk) {
  41:             auditLogger.denied(plugin.manifest.id, "cleartext_in_release", url)
  42:             throw PluginBridgeException("cleartext_in_release", "fetch URL must be HTTPS")
  43:         }
  44:         if (!EndpointMatcher.matches(url, plugin.manifest.declaredEndpoints)) {
  45:             auditLogger.denied(plugin.manifest.id, "endpoint_not_declared", url)
  46:             throw PluginBridgeException("endpoint_not_declared", "Endpoint not declared: $url")
  47:         }
  48: 
  49:         val init = args["init"] as? Map<*, *>
  50:         val method = (init?.get("method") as? String)?.uppercase() ?: "GET"
  51:         val body = init?.get("body") as? String
  52:         val mediaType = (init?.get("contentType") as? String)?.toMediaTypeOrNull()
  53:         val requestBody = if (body != null && method !in setOf("GET", "HEAD")) body.toRequestBody(mediaType) else null
  54:         val builder = Request.Builder().url(url).method(method, requestBody)
  55:         (init?.get("headers") as? Map<*, *>)?.forEach { (name, value) ->
  56:             if (name is String && value is String) builder.header(name, value)
  57:         }
  58: 
  59:         client.newCall(builder.build()).execute().use { response ->
  60:             JsonBridgeCodec.toJson(
  61:                 mapOf(
  62:                     "status" to response.code,
  63:                     "headers" to response.headers.toMultimap().mapValues { it.value.joinToString(",") },
  64:                     "body" to (response.body?.string() ?: ""),
  65:                 ),
  66:             )
  67:         }
  68:     }

   5:  * Error raised when a URL does not match the plugin manifest endpoint allowlist.

   7: export class EndpointNotDeclaredError extends Error {
   8:   /** URL rejected before reaching the native bridge. */
   9:   readonly url: string;
  10: 
  11:   constructor(url: string) {
  12:     super(`Endpoint is not declared by plugin manifest: ${url}`);

  16: }
  17: 
  18: /**
  19:  * Typed wrapper for `platform.network`.
  20:  */
  21: export const network = {
  22:   /**
  23:    * Fetches a URL through the host bridge after checking the manifest endpoint allowlist.
  24:    */
  25:   async fetch(url: string, init?: RequestInit): Promise<Response> {
  26:     assertEndpointDeclared(url);
  27:     return await callPlatform('network.fetch', (bridge) => bridge.network.fetch(url, init));
  28:   },

  30: 
  31: /**
  32:  * Returns true when a URL matches at least one declared endpoint pattern.
  33:  */
  34: export function isEndpointDeclared(url: string, patterns: readonly string[]): boolean {
  35:   return patterns.some((pattern) => endpointPatternToRegExp(pattern).test(url));
  36: }
  37: 
  38: /**
  39:  * Throws `EndpointNotDeclaredError` when the active plugin manifest does not declare a URL.
  40:  */
  41: export function assertEndpointDeclared(url: string): void {
  42:   const manifest = getRegisteredManifest();
  43:   if (!manifest || !isEndpointDeclared(url, manifest.declaredEndpoints)) {
  44:     throw new EndpointNotDeclaredError(url);
  45:   }
  46: }
  47: 
  48: function endpointPatternToRegExp(pattern: string): RegExp {
  49:   const pathStart = findPathStart(pattern);
  50:   let source = '';
  51: 
  52:   for (let index = 0; index < pattern.length; index += 1) {
  53:     const character = pattern[index];
  54:     if (character === '*') {
  55:       source += index < pathStart ? '[^./]*' : '[^/]*';
  56:     } else {
  57:       source += escapeRegExp(character);
  58:     }
  59:   }
  60: 
  61:   return new RegExp(`^${source}$`);
  62: }
  63: 
  64: function findPathStart(pattern: string): number {
  65:   const schemeEnd = pattern.indexOf('://');
  66:   const searchFrom = schemeEnd === -1 ? 0 : schemeEnd + 3;
  67:   const slash = pattern.indexOf('/', searchFrom);
  68:   return slash === -1 ? pattern.length : slash;
  69: }
  70: 
  71: function escapeRegExp(character: string | undefined): string {
  72:   if (!character) return '';
  73:   return /[.+?^${}()|[\]\\]/.test(character) ? `\\${character}` : character;
  74: }

   1: package app.syncler.feature.inbox
   2: 
   3: import android.webkit.JavascriptInterface
   4: import android.webkit.WebView
   5: import app.syncler.feature.inbox.BuildConfig
   6: import kotlinx.coroutines.CoroutineScope
   7: import kotlinx.coroutines.Dispatchers
   8: import kotlinx.coroutines.SupervisorJob
   9: import kotlinx.coroutines.cancel
  10: import kotlinx.coroutines.launch
  11: import kotlinx.coroutines.withContext
  12: import okhttp3.ConnectionSpec
  13: import okhttp3.CookieJar
  14: import okhttp3.MediaType.Companion.toMediaTypeOrNull
  15: import okhttp3.OkHttpClient
  16: import okhttp3.Request
  17: import okhttp3.RequestBody.Companion.toRequestBody
  18: import org.json.JSONObject
  19: 
  20: /**
  21:  * Minimal native bridge for inbox-rendered cards. Exposed to the WebView as
  22:  * `window.__syncler_native__`; the shell HTML wraps it in a `window.platform`
  23:  * proxy that mirrors the SDK contract.
  24:  *
  25:  * Only `platform.network.fetch` is wired ג€” the lottery dogfood's "Played"
  26:  * button needs it, and that's the only capability V1 senders rely on. Other
  27:  * methods (storage, camera, notifications, ג€¦) explicitly reject so plugins
  28:  * fail loudly instead of silently no-op'ing. Wiring the full bridge is the
  29:  * next chunk, and it should reuse `:feature:plugin-host`'s bridges rather
  30:  * than re-implement them here.
  31:  */
  32: class CardBridge(
  33:     private val webView: WebView,
  34:     private val declaredEndpoints: List<String>,
  35: ) {
  36:     private val scope = CoroutineScope(SupervisorJob() + Dispatchers.IO)
  37:     private val httpClient = OkHttpClient.Builder()
  38:         .cookieJar(CookieJar.NO_COOKIES)
  39:         .connectionSpecs(
  40:             if (BuildConfig.DEBUG) {
  41:                 listOf(ConnectionSpec.MODERN_TLS, ConnectionSpec.CLEARTEXT)
  42:             } else {
  43:                 listOf(ConnectionSpec.MODERN_TLS)
  44:             },
  45:         )
  46:         .build()
  47: 
  48:     @JavascriptInterface
  49:     fun call(method: String, argsJson: String, callbackId: String) {
  50:         scope.launch {
  51:             val result = runCatching { dispatch(method, argsJson) }
  52:             val payload = if (result.isSuccess) {
  53:                 """{"success":true,"value":${result.getOrThrow()}}"""
  54:             } else {
  55:                 val message = result.exceptionOrNull()?.message ?: "card bridge error"
  56:                 """{"success":false,"error":"call_failed","message":${JSONObject.quote(message)}}"""
  57:             }
  58:             webView.post {
  59:                 webView.evaluateJavascript(
  60:                     "window.__syncler_internal_callback(${JSONObject.quote(callbackId)}, $payload)",
  61:                     null,
  62:                 )
  63:             }
  64:         }
  65:     }
  66: 
  67:     fun destroy() {
  68:         scope.cancel()
  69:     }
  70: 
  71:     private suspend fun dispatch(method: String, argsJson: String): String = when (method) {
  72:         "platform.network.fetch" -> doFetch(argsJson)
  73:         else -> throw UnsupportedOperationException("$method is not wired in inbox mode")
  74:     }
  75: 
  76:     private suspend fun doFetch(argsJson: String): String = withContext(Dispatchers.IO) {
  77:         val args = JSONObject(argsJson)
  78:         val url = args.optString("url").ifBlank { throw IllegalArgumentException("missing url") }
  79:         // Scheme check (defense in depth ג€” the OkHttp client already refuses
  80:         // cleartext in release via its connectionSpecs, but failing explicitly
  81:         // here gives a clearer error and survives future client wiring drift).
  82:         val schemeOk = url.startsWith("https://") || (BuildConfig.DEBUG && url.startsWith("http://"))
  83:         if (!schemeOk) throw SecurityException("fetch URL must be HTTPS: $url")
  84:         if (!matchesAny(url, declaredEndpoints)) {
  85:             throw SecurityException("endpoint not declared: $url")
  86:         }
  87:         val init = args.optJSONObject("init")
  88:         val method = init?.optString("method")?.uppercase()?.takeIf { it.isNotBlank() } ?: "GET"
  89:         val bodyText = init?.optString("body")?.takeIf { it.isNotBlank() && method !in setOf("GET", "HEAD") }
  90:         val mediaType = init?.optString("contentType")?.takeIf { it.isNotBlank() }?.toMediaTypeOrNull()
  91:         val request = Request.Builder().url(url).method(method, bodyText?.toRequestBody(mediaType)).apply {
  92:             init?.optJSONObject("headers")?.let { headers ->
  93:                 headers.keys().forEach { key -> header(key, headers.optString(key)) }
  94:             }
  95:         }.build()
  96: 
  97:         httpClient.newCall(request).execute().use { response ->
  98:             val responseBody = response.body?.string().orEmpty()
  99:             val headersJson = JSONObject().also { h ->
 100:                 response.headers.names().forEach { name ->
 101:                     h.put(name, response.headers(name).joinToString(","))
 102:                 }
 103:             }
 104:             JSONObject()
 105:                 .put("status", response.code)
 106:                 .put("headers", headersJson)
 107:                 .put("body", responseBody)
 108:                 .toString()
 109:         }
 110:     }
 111: 
 112:     private fun matchesAny(url: String, patterns: List<String>): Boolean =
 113:         patterns.any { pattern -> endpointPatternToRegex(pattern).matches(url) }
 114: 
 115:     // Same logic as :feature:plugin-host's EndpointMatcher; inlined here so
 116:     // :feature:inbox doesn't need to depend on the whole plugin-host module
 117:     // graph just for this glob match.
 118:     private fun endpointPatternToRegex(pattern: String): Regex {
 119:         val pathStart = findPathStart(pattern)
 120:         val source = buildString {
 121:             pattern.forEachIndexed { index, character ->
 122:                 if (character == '*') {
 123:                     append(if (index < pathStart) "[^./]*" else "[^/]*")
 124:                 } else {
 125:                     append(Regex.escape(character.toString()))
 126:                 }
 127:             }
 128:         }
 129:         return Regex("^$source$")
 130:     }
 131: 
 132:     private fun findPathStart(pattern: String): Int {
 133:         val schemeEnd = pattern.indexOf("://")
 134:         val searchFrom = if (schemeEnd == -1) 0 else schemeEnd + 3
 135:         val slash = pattern.indexOf('/', searchFrom)
 136:         return if (slash == -1) pattern.length else slash
 137:     }
 138: 
 139:     companion object {
 140:         const val NATIVE_BRIDGE_NAME = "__syncler_native__"
 141:     }
 142: }

  30: /**
  31:  * Plugin metadata consumed by the native host before loading a bundle.

  33: export interface PluginManifest {
  34:   /** Reverse-DNS plugin identifier, for example `com.example.plugin`. */
  35:   id: string;
  36:   /** Human-readable plugin name. */
  37:   name: string;
  38:   /** Semantic plugin version. */
  39:   version: string;
  40:   /** Sender identifier associated with inbound encrypted messages. */
  41:   senderId: string;
  42:   /** Lowercase or uppercase hexadecimal hash of the JavaScript bundle. */
  43:   bundleHash: string;
  44:   /** Lowercase or uppercase hexadecimal Ed25519 signature. */
  45:   signature: string;
  46:   /** Capabilities the plugin is allowed to use at runtime. */
  47:   declaredCapabilities: Capability[];
  48:   /** Allowed URL patterns for `platform.network.fetch`. */
  49:   declaredEndpoints: string[];
  50:   /** Host dismissal behavior for notifications created by this plugin. */
  51:   dismissBehavior: DismissBehavior;
  52:   /** Minimum compatible native bridge version. */
  53:   minPlatformVersion: string;
  54:   /**
  55:    * Render mode. `'script'` (default) loads the JS bundle in a WebView.
  56:    * `'template'` ships no JS and uses a native Compose card driven by
  57:    * [template]. Server defaults to `'script'` when omitted.
  58:    */
  59:   renderer?: 'script' | 'template';
  60:   /**
  61:    * Template manifest. Required when [renderer] is `'template'`; rejected
  62:    * when [renderer] is `'script'`. Validated server-side at publish time.
  63:    */
  64:   template?: TemplateBlock;
  65:   /**
  66:    * Card delivery semantics. `'event'` (default) ג€” each send is a new
  67:    * immutable inbox row. `'live'` ג€” persistent, upsertable; see
  68:    * `docs/integration-guide.md ֲ§5.2`. Server defaults to `'event'`.
  69:    */
  70:   cardType?: 'event' | 'live';
  71:   /**
  72:    * JSONPath into the decrypted payload that yields the stable card
  73:    * identity. REQUIRED when [cardType] is `'live'`; rejected otherwise.
  74:    * V1 validates only `startsWith("$")` server-side.
  75:    */
  76:   cardKeyPath?: string;
  77: }

  79: /**
  80:  * Error raised when plugin manifest validation fails.
  81:  */
  82: export class ManifestValidationError extends Error {
  83:   /** Individual validation failures. */
  84:   readonly issues: string[];
  85: 
  86:   constructor(issues: string[]) {
  87:     super(`Invalid plugin manifest: ${issues.join('; ')}`);
  88:     this.name = 'ManifestValidationError';
  89:     this.issues = issues;
  90:   }
  91: }

  93: const idPattern = /^[a-zA-Z][a-zA-Z0-9-]*(\.[a-zA-Z][a-zA-Z0-9-]*)+$/;
  94: const semverPattern = /^(0|[1-9]\d*)\.(0|[1-9]\d*)\.(0|[1-9]\d*)(?:-[0-9A-Za-z.-]+)?(?:\+[0-9A-Za-z.-]+)?$/;
  95: const hexPattern = /^[0-9a-fA-F]+$/;
  96: const allCapabilities = new Set<string>(Object.values(Capability));
  97: const allDismissBehaviors = new Set<string>(Object.values(DismissBehavior));

 101: /**
 102:  * Returns true when `value` is a valid plugin manifest.
 103:  */
 104: export function isPluginManifest(value: unknown): value is PluginManifest {
 105:   return validatePluginManifest(value).valid;
 106: }
 107: 
 108: /**
 109:  * Validates unknown JSON-like data as a `PluginManifest`.
 110:  */
 111: export function validatePluginManifest(value: unknown): { valid: true; manifest: PluginManifest } | { valid: false; issues: string[] } {
 112:   const issues: string[] = [];
 113: 
 114:   if (!isRecord(value)) {
 115:     return { valid: false, issues: ['manifest must be an object'] };
 116:   }
 117: 
 118:   requireString(value, 'id', issues, (id) => {
 119:     if (!idPattern.test(id)) issues.push('id must be reverse-DNS format');
 120:   });
 121:   requireString(value, 'name', issues);
 122:   requireString(value, 'version', issues, (version) => {
 123:     if (!semverPattern.test(version)) issues.push('version must be semver');
 124:   });
 125:   requireString(value, 'senderId', issues);
 126:   requireString(value, 'bundleHash', issues, (hash) => {
 127:     if (!hexPattern.test(hash)) issues.push('bundleHash must be hex');
 128:   });
 129:   requireString(value, 'signature', issues, (signature) => {
 130:     if (!hexPattern.test(signature)) issues.push('signature must be hex');
 131:   });
 132:   requireString(value, 'minPlatformVersion', issues, (version) => {
 133:     if (!semverPattern.test(version)) issues.push('minPlatformVersion must be semver');
 134:   });
 135: 
 136:   // renderer + template pairing. Both are optional; server defaults
 137:   // renderer to 'script'. When present, renderer must be one of the
 138:   // two enum values, and template/script ג†” template-present pairing
 139:   // is enforced strictly (matches server's
 140:   // PluginPublishRequest.validate_renderer_template_pairing).
 141:   const renderer = value.renderer;
 142:   if (renderer !== undefined && renderer !== 'script' && renderer !== 'template') {
 143:     issues.push('renderer must be "script" or "template" when set');
 144:   }
 145:   const effectiveRenderer = renderer ?? 'script';
 146:   if (effectiveRenderer === 'template' && !value.template) {
 147:     issues.push('template required when renderer is "template"');
 148:   }
 149:   if (effectiveRenderer === 'script' && value.template !== undefined && value.template !== null) {
 150:     issues.push('template must be omitted when renderer is "script"');
 151:   }
 152: 
 153:   // cardType + cardKeyPath pairing. Same defaulting rules ג€” optional in
 154:   // the SDK, server defaults to 'event'. cardKeyPath is required iff
 155:   // cardType is 'live'.
 156:   const cardType = value.cardType;
 157:   if (cardType !== undefined && cardType !== 'event' && cardType !== 'live') {
 158:     issues.push('cardType must be "event" or "live" when set');
 159:   }
 160:   const effectiveCardType = cardType ?? 'event';
 161:   if (effectiveCardType === 'live' && !value.cardKeyPath) {
 162:     issues.push('cardKeyPath required when cardType is "live"');
 163:   }
 164:   if (effectiveCardType === 'event' && value.cardKeyPath !== undefined && value.cardKeyPath !== null) {
 165:     issues.push('cardKeyPath must be omitted when cardType is "event"');
 166:   }
 167:   if (
 168:     effectiveCardType === 'live' &&
 169:     typeof value.cardKeyPath === 'string' &&
 170:     !value.cardKeyPath.startsWith('$')
 171:   ) {
 172:     issues.push('cardKeyPath must begin with "$"');
 173:   }
 174: 
 175:   if (!Array.isArray(value.declaredCapabilities)) {
 176:     issues.push('declaredCapabilities must be an array');
 177:   } else {
 178:     for (const capability of value.declaredCapabilities) {
 179:       if (typeof capability !== 'string' || !allCapabilities.has(capability)) {
 180:         issues.push(`unknown capability: ${String(capability)}`);
 181:       }
 182:     }
 183:   }
 184: 
 185:   if (!Array.isArray(value.declaredEndpoints)) {
 186:     issues.push('declaredEndpoints must be an array');
 187:   } else {
 188:     for (const endpoint of value.declaredEndpoints) {
 189:       if (typeof endpoint !== 'string' || endpoint.length === 0) {
 190:         issues.push('declaredEndpoints entries must be non-empty strings');
 191:       }
 192:     }
 193:   }
 194: 
 195:   if (typeof value.dismissBehavior !== 'string' || !allDismissBehaviors.has(value.dismissBehavior)) {
 196:     issues.push('dismissBehavior must be a known dismiss behavior');
 197:   }
 198: 
 199:   if (issues.length > 0) {
 200:     return { valid: false, issues };
 201:   }
 202: 
 203:   return { valid: true, manifest: value as unknown as PluginManifest };
 204: }
 205: 
 206: /**
 207:  * Validates a manifest and throws `ManifestValidationError` when invalid.
 208:  */
 209: export function assertPluginManifest(value: unknown): asserts value is PluginManifest {
 210:   const result = validatePluginManifest(value);
 211:   if (!result.valid) {
 212:     throw new ManifestValidationError(result.issues);
 213:   }
 214: }
 215: 
 216: /**
 217:  * Returns the manifest registered for the currently loaded plugin, if any.
 218:  */
 219: export function getRegisteredManifest(): PluginManifest | undefined {
 220:   return activeManifest;
 221: }

 224:  * Stores the manifest for SDK runtime checks performed after plugin registration.
 225:  *
 226:  * @internal
 227:  */
 228: export function setRegisteredManifest(manifest: PluginManifest | undefined): void {
 229:   activeManifest = manifest;

 232: function requireString(
 233:   record: Record<string, unknown>,
 234:   key: keyof PluginManifest,
 235:   issues: string[],
 236:   validate?: (value: string) => void,
 237: ): void {
 238:   const value = record[key];
 239:   if (typeof value !== 'string' || value.length === 0) {
 240:     issues.push(`${String(key)} must be a non-empty string`);
 241:     return;
 242:   }
 243:   validate?.(value);
 244: }

 247:   return typeof value === 'object' && value !== null && !Array.isArray(value);
 248: }

   1: # syncler (Python sender SDK)
   2: 
   3: Send messages from your backend into the Syncler platform.
   4: 
   5: ## Install
   6: 
   7: ```sh
   8: pip install syncler
   9: ```
  10: 
  11: ## Quickstart
  12: 
  13: ```python
  14: from syncler import Client
  15: 
  16: client = Client(
  17:     sender_name="Trading Bot",
  18:     private_key_path="~/.syncler/keys/trading.pem",
  19:     base_url="https://api.syncler.app",
  20: )
  21: 
  22: # Once: register the sender's public key. Persist the returned sender_id.
  23: sender_id = client.register_if_needed(contact="ops@example.com")
  24: print("Save this:", sender_id)
  25: 
  26: # Or on subsequent runs:
  27: client.set_sender_id("the-saved-sender-id")
  28: 
  29: # Pair with a user (one-time per user-device).
  30: qr_path = client.create_pairing_qr(ttl_seconds=300)
  31: print(f"Show this QR to the user: {qr_path}")
  32: # Once the user pairs in their Syncler app, they'll get a confirmation
  33: # screen showing your sender's fingerprint. They confirm. You need their
  34: # user_id + pairing_key from the device-side exchange (M7 wires this; for
  35: # now in dev, use client.set_pairing(user_id, pairing_key)).
  36: 
  37: client.set_pairing(user_id="...", pairing_key=b"...32-bytes-shared-secret...")
  38: 
  39: # Send a message.
  40: result = client.send_to(
  41:     user_uuid=client._latest_pairing.user_id,
  42:     plugin_identifier="com.trading.app",
  43:     plugin_id="row-uuid-of-published-version",
  44:     payload={"pnl": 1234.56, "trades": 7},
  45:     min_plugin_version="1.0.0",
  46: )
  47: print(f"Sent {result.message_id}, expires {result.expires_at}")
  48: ```
  49: 
  50: ## Publishing a plugin
  51: 
  52: ```python
  53: import hashlib
  54: 
  55: bundle_bytes = open("path/to/plugin.bundle.js", "rb").read()
  56: bundle_hash = hashlib.sha256(bundle_bytes).digest()
  57: 
  58: # manifest_hash is the SHA-256 of the canonical manifest JSON; the
  59: # bundle_signature is the Ed25519 signature over canonical_manifest
  60: # + bundleHash bytes (see docs/crypto-spec.md ֲ§5).
  61: response = client.publish_plugin(
  62:     plugin_identifier="com.trading.app",
  63:     version="1.0.0",
  64:     manifest_hash=manifest_hash,
  65:     bundle_hash=bundle_hash,
  66:     bundle_signature=bundle_signature,
  67:     signed_bundle_url="https://your-cdn.com/plugin.bundle.js",
  68:     capabilities=["network"],
  69:     endpoints=["https://your-backend.com/api/*"],
  70: )
  71: print("Published version row:", response["plugin_row_id"])
  72: ```
  73: 
  74: ## Threading
  75: 
  76: The client is sync. Wrap calls in your own thread pool / asyncio executor
  77: if you need concurrent sends.
  78: 
  79: ## Spec
  80: 
  81: See `docs/crypto-spec.md` (top of repo) for the canonical AAD + envelope
  82: shapes. The SDK is the reference Python implementation.

  18: 
  19: class PluginBridge(
  20:     private val plugin: PluginInstance,
  21:     private val webViewProvider: () -> WebView?,
  22:     private val scope: CoroutineScope,
  23:     private val networkBridge: NetworkBridge,
  24:     private val storageBridge: StorageBridge,
  25:     private val notificationBridge: NotificationBridge,
  26:     private val cameraBridge: CameraBridge,
  27:     private val galleryBridge: GalleryBridge,
  28:     private val fileBridge: FileBridge,
  29:     private val locationBridge: LocationBridge,
  30:     private val messageBridge: MessageBridge,
  31:     private val auditLogger: AuditLogger,
  32: ) {
  33:     private val mainHandler = Handler(Looper.getMainLooper())
  34: 
  35:     @JavascriptInterface
  36:     fun call(method: String, argsJson: String, callbackId: String) {
  37:         scope.launch {
  38:             val resultJson = runCatching {
  39:                 withTimeout(CALL_TIMEOUT_MS) {
  40:                     bridgeSuccessJson(dispatch(method, argsJson))
  41:                 }
  42:             }.getOrElse { error ->
  43:                 val reason = when (error) {
  44:                     is kotlinx.coroutines.TimeoutCancellationException -> "timeout"
  45:                     is PluginBridgeException -> error.code
  46:                     else -> "bridge_error"
  47:                 }
  48:                 auditLogger.denied(plugin.manifest.id, reason, method)
  49:                 bridgeErrorJson(reason, error.message ?: reason)
  50:             }
  51:             deliver(callbackId, resultJson)
  52:         }
  53:     }
  54: 
  55:     private suspend fun dispatch(method: String, argsJson: String): String {
  56:         val capability = requiredCapability(method)
  57:         if (capability != null && capability !in plugin.grantedCapabilities) {
  58:             auditLogger.denied(plugin.manifest.id, "capability_not_granted", capability)
  59:             throw PluginBridgeException("capability_not_granted", "Capability not granted: $capability")
  60:         }
  61: 
  62:         return when (method) {
  63:             "platform.network.fetch" -> networkBridge.fetch(plugin, argsJson)
  64:             "platform.storage.get" -> storageBridge.get(plugin, argsJson)
  65:             "platform.storage.set" -> storageBridge.set(plugin, argsJson)
  66:             "platform.storage.delete" -> storageBridge.delete(plugin, argsJson)
  67:             "platform.showNotification" -> notificationBridge.show(plugin, argsJson)
  68:             "platform.camera.capture" -> cameraBridge.capture(plugin, argsJson)
  69:             "platform.gallery.pick" -> galleryBridge.pick(plugin, argsJson)
  70:             "platform.file.pick" -> fileBridge.pick(plugin, argsJson)
  71:             "platform.location.current" -> locationBridge.current(plugin, argsJson)
  72:             "platform.message.respond" -> messageBridge.respond(plugin, argsJson)
  73:             "platform.message.dismissBehavior" -> messageBridge.dismissBehavior(plugin, argsJson)
  74:             else -> {
  75:                 auditLogger.denied(plugin.manifest.id, "unknown_method", method)
  76:                 throw PluginBridgeException("unknown_method", "Unknown bridge method: $method")
  77:             }
  78:         }
  79:     }
  80: 
  81:     private fun deliver(callbackId: String, resultJson: String) {
  82:         val script = "window.__syncler_internal_callback(${JsonEscaping.quote(callbackId)}, $resultJson)"
  83:         mainHandler.post {
  84:             runCatching { webViewProvider()?.evaluateJavascript(script, null) }
  85:                 .onFailure { auditLogger.denied(plugin.manifest.id, "callback_delivery_failed", it.message) }
  86:         }
  87:     }
  88: 
  89:     companion object {
  90:         const val NATIVE_BRIDGE_NAME = "__syncler_native__"
  91:         const val CALL_TIMEOUT_MS = 30_000L
  92:     }
  93: }
  94: 
  95: internal fun requiredCapability(method: String): String? = when {
  96:     method.startsWith("platform.network.") -> "network"
  97:     method.startsWith("platform.storage.") -> "storage"
  98:     method.startsWith("platform.camera.") -> "camera"
  99:     method.startsWith("platform.gallery.") -> "gallery"
 100:     method.startsWith("platform.file.") -> "file"
 101:     method.startsWith("platform.location.") -> "location"
 102:     method == "platform.showNotification" -> null
 103:     method.startsWith("platform.message.") -> null
 104:     else -> null
 105: }

 107: internal fun bridgeSuccessJson(valueJson: String): String =
 108:     """{"success":true,"value":$valueJson}"""
 109: 
 110: internal fun bridgeErrorJson(error: String, message: String): String =
 111:     """{"success":false,"error":${JsonEscaping.quote(error)},"message":${JsonEscaping.quote(message)}}"""

   1: # Syncler Plugin SDK
   2: 
   3: TypeScript SDK for Syncler WebView plugins. Native bridge implementation is provided by the host application.
   4: 
   5: ## Install
   6: 
   7: ```sh
   8: npm install
   9: ```
  10: 
  11: ## Build
  12: 
  13: ```sh
  14: npm run build
  15: ```
  16: 
  17: ## Test
  18: 
  19: ```sh
  20: npm test
  21: ```
  22: 
  23: ## Minimal Plugin
  24: 
  25: ```ts
  26: import { BasePlugin, DismissBehavior, registerPlugin } from '@syncler/plugin-sdk';
  27: 
  28: export class MinimalPlugin extends BasePlugin {
  29:   static manifest = {
  30:     id: 'com.example.minimal',
  31:     name: 'Minimal',
  32:     version: '1.0.0',
  33:     senderId: 'com.example.sender',
  34:     bundleHash: '00',
  35:     signature: '00',
  36:     declaredCapabilities: [],
  37:     declaredEndpoints: [],
  38:     dismissBehavior: DismissBehavior.DISMISS_LOCAL_ONLY,
  39:     minPlatformVersion: '1.0.0',
  40:   };
  41: 
  42:   render(data: { text: string }) {
  43:     return `<div>${data.text}</div>`;
  44:   }
  45: }
  46: 
  47: registerPlugin(new MinimalPlugin());
  48: ```
  49: 
  50: Build the example bundle:
  51: 
  52: ```sh
  53: npm run build:example
  54: ```
  55: 
  56: The native host calls `__syncler_internal_dispatch(hook, args)` after loading the plugin bundle. Plugin bundles should register exactly one plugin instance with `registerPlugin`.
  57: 
  58: ## Bridge Wrappers
  59: 
  60: - `storage.get/set/delete` forwards to `platform.storage`.
  61: - `network.fetch` checks `manifest.declaredEndpoints` before calling `platform.network.fetch`.
  62: - `showNotification` and `notifications.show` forward to `platform.showNotification`.
  63: 
  64: Endpoint patterns support `*` as a single path or host segment wildcard. For example, `https://api.example.com/v1/*` matches one path segment under `/v1/`, and `https://*.example.com/feed` matches one host segment.
  65: 
  66: ## Signing
  67: 
  68: `tools/sign-bundle.ts` computes a SHA-256 bundle hash and Ed25519 signature over the JavaScript bundle:
  69: 
  70: ```sh
  71: npx tsx tools/sign-bundle.ts examples/minimal/dist/plugin.bundle.js private_key.pem examples/minimal/manifest.json
  72: ```

   5: /**
   6:  * Builds the per-card WebView HTML shell.
   7:  *
   8:  * The shell:
   9:  *  1. Installs a `window.platform` proxy that round-trips through the native
  10:  *     `__syncler_native__` JavascriptInterface (see [CardBridge]). For V1
  11:  *     inbox mode only `platform.network.fetch` is wired native-side; other
  12:  *     methods reject with a clear error so plugins fail visibly rather than
  13:  *     silently no-op'ing.
  14:  *  2. Runs the plugin bundle (IIFE; self-registers via `registerPlugin(...)`).
  15:  *  3. Dispatches the `render` hook with the message payload, injects the
  16:  *     returned HTML into the body, and re-creates any inline `<script>` tags
  17:  *     so click handlers (e.g. lottery's "Played" button) wire up.
  18:  */
  19: internal object RenderShell {
  20:     fun build(bundleJs: String, payloadJson: String): String {
  21:         // Defensive: the bundle's source may contain literal `</script>` (e.g.
  22:         // in a quoted string). Break the sequence so the host's `<script>`
  23:         // closer doesn't get prematurely matched by the HTML parser.
  24:         val safeBundle = bundleJs.replace("</script", "<\\/script", ignoreCase = true)
  25:         val safePayloadWrap = JSONObject().put("p", payloadJson).toString()
  26:             .replace("</script", "<\\/script", ignoreCase = true)
  27:         return """
  28:             <!doctype html>
  29:             <html>
  30:             <head>
  31:               <meta charset="utf-8">
  32:               <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width,initial-scale=1">
  33:               <style>
  34:                 html, body { margin: 0; padding: 0; }
  35:                 body { font-family: -apple-system, Roboto, sans-serif; color: #1c1b1f; background: transparent; }
  36:                 #syncler-render-error { color: #b3261e; padding: 12px; font-size: 13px; }
  37:               </style>
  38:             </head>
  39:             <body>
  40:               <script>
  41:               // Capture uncaught errors that fire during bundle execution.
  42:               // WebView <script> tags swallow throws and move on to the next
  43:               // block, so without this hook a manifest-validation failure (or
  44:               // any other top-level throw) is invisible ג€” the symptom you'd
  45:               // see is the *next* error ("No Syncler plugin has been
  46:               // registered") instead of the real root cause.
  47:               window.__syncler_bundleLoadErrors = [];
  48:               window.addEventListener('error', (ev) => {
  49:                 window.__syncler_bundleLoadErrors.push(
  50:                   (ev.error && ev.error.message) || ev.message || 'unknown error'
  51:                 );
  52:               });
  53:               window.addEventListener('unhandledrejection', (ev) => {
  54:                 const reason = ev.reason;
  55:                 window.__syncler_bundleLoadErrors.push(
  56:                   (reason && reason.message) || String(reason)
  57:                 );
  58:               });
  59:               </script>
  60:               <script>
  61:               (() => {
  62:                 const callbacks = new Map();
  63:                 let nextCallbackId = 1;
  64:                 window.__syncler_internal_callback = (callbackId, result) => {
  65:                   const callback = callbacks.get(callbackId);
  66:                   if (!callback) return;
  67:                   callbacks.delete(callbackId);
  68:                   if (result && result.success) callback.resolve(result.value);
  69:                   else callback.reject(new Error((result && (result.message || result.error)) || 'unknown_error'));
  70:                 };
  71:                 const nativeCall = (method, args) => new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
  72:                   const callbackId = String(nextCallbackId++);
  73:                   callbacks.set(callbackId, { resolve, reject });
  74:                   window.__syncler_native__.call(method, JSON.stringify(args || {}), callbackId);
  75:                 });
  76:                 const asResponse = async (payload) => new Response(payload.body || '', {
  77:                   status: payload.status || 200,
  78:                   headers: payload.headers || {}
  79:                 });
  80:                 const reject = (name) => () => Promise.reject(new Error(
  81:                   'platform.' + name + ' is not wired in V1 inbox mode'));
  82:                 window.platform = {
  83:                   __version__: '1.0.0',
  84:                   showNotification: reject('showNotification'),
  85:                   storage: { get: reject('storage.get'), set: reject('storage.set'), delete: reject('storage.delete') },
  86:                   network: {
  87:                     fetch: (url, init) => nativeCall('platform.network.fetch', { url, init }).then(asResponse)
  88:                   },
  89:                   camera: { capture: reject('camera.capture') },
  90:                   gallery: { pick: reject('gallery.pick') },
  91:                   file: { pick: reject('file.pick') },
  92:                   location: { current: reject('location.current') },
  93:                   message: {
  94:                     respond: reject('message.respond'),
  95:                     dismissBehavior: () => undefined
  96:                   }
  97:                 };
  98:               })();
  99:               </script>
 100:               <script>$safeBundle</script>
 101:               <script>
 102:               (async () => {
 103:                 try {
 104:                   // If the bundle threw at load time, surface that ג€” its real
 105:                   // message is far more useful than the generic

 107:                   const loadErrors = window.__syncler_bundleLoadErrors || [];

.\docs\ROADMAP.md:14:- [x] Host-owned plugin settings sheet (sender mute, pairing revoke). Sender-side plugin-row revoke (`client.revoke_plugin(...)`) is a separate published-side API; the host UI exposes pairing revoke, not plugin-row revoke.
.\docs\ROADMAP.md:18:## V1.5 — Plugin runtime + key hygiene
.\docs\ROADMAP.md:22:3. **Master-key rotation.** UX + protocol for rotating the user's 32-byte master key without losing access to historical state. Required before per-device encryption (#4) lands.
.\docs\ROADMAP.md:23:4. **Per-device envelope encryption.** Senders encrypt the payload separately for each of the user's enrolled devices, keyed by per-device public keys instead of the shared user master key. Enables forward secrecy and immediate per-device revocation without rotating user-wide keys.
.\docs\ROADMAP.md:24:5. **Durable nonce-replay protection.** Move the per-sender nonce registry from in-memory to Postgres so a worker restart can't accept a replayed envelope.
.\docs\ROADMAP.md:42:14. **Guided lost-device rotation flow.** Click-through UX for: revoke lost device → re-pair on trusted devices → rotate master key (depends on V1.5 #3). Today the user does steps 1–2 by hand; this automates the sequence.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:36:- **Per-device dismiss (server-side filter).** When the user dismisses a message on device A, `/v1/messages/{id}/dismiss` writes a `DeliveryStatus` row keyed on `(message_id, device_id=A)`. Subsequent calls to `/v1/messages/inbox` from device A LEFT JOIN `DeliveryStatus` for `device_id=A` and filter rows where `dismissed_at IS NOT NULL` out of A's feed. The dismiss SSE event still fans out to *all* of the user's devices, but the server-side filter is per-device — devices B, C, etc. receive the hint and refresh, but their own feeds keep the row until they dismiss it themselves. V1 design: dismiss is a per-device gesture (some users want a card visible elsewhere); cross-device "dismiss everywhere" is a V1.5 add.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:74:`searchText` is folded into the host's inbox search alongside title, subtitle, summary, and sender name. The host does a case-insensitive substring match — populate this with the terms a user would type into the search box but that aren't part of the visible row (ticker symbols, ticket numbers, account references). Plugin-scoped *content* search (a search bar that runs against your backend) is V1.5.

.\README.md:33:- **Server is content-blind.** Every byte of message content is encrypted with a per-pairing AES-256-GCM key derived client-side from a 256-bit master key. The master key is wrapped by an Argon2id-derived key from the user's password (Bitwarden/ProtonMail zero-knowledge pattern). The server stores only: account hashes, encrypted master key blobs, encrypted message bodies, encrypted user state, plugin metadata, and signing keys (public only).
.\README.md:35:- **Multi-device** with optimistic-concurrency state sync. User accounts unlock from any device with email + password; the per-device plugin install state, pairings, and dismissal state sync as an encrypted blob.
.\README.md:36:- **Cryptographic identity for senders** via Ed25519. Every message envelope is signed; every plugin bundle is signed. The phone locks the sender's public-key fingerprint + name + name hash at pairing time, so impersonation is prevented at multiple layers.
.\README.md:83:See [sdk-python/README.md](sdk-python/README.md) for the full pairing + send + publish flow.
.\README.md:105:- **`wait_for_pairing` in the Python SDK** raises NotImplementedError — needs a server-side "did this pairing token complete?" poll endpoint.
.\README.md:106:- **Per-key user-scoped storage sync** with timestamps/tombstones — deferred to V1.5; documented data-loss risk.
.\README.md:107:- **QR camera scanning** in pairing — V1 uses paste-URL flow; camera is M11.
.\README.md:108:- **Marketplace** for plugin distribution — V1 uses sideload (URL install). Marketplace is V1.5.
.\server\README.md:72:The process deletes expired messages, revoked pairings older than 180 days, and stale rate limit events. Schedule it outside the app process, for example with AWS EventBridge or a systemd timer.
.\server\README.md:76:When deploying the server behind a reverse proxy (e.g., Nginx, Traefik, AWS ALB), it is critical to configure the proxy correctly. The application relies on the `X-Forwarded-For` and `X-Forwarded-Host` headers to determine the client's IP address (for rate limiting) and the public-facing hostname (for generating pairing URLs).
.\server\README.md:78:Ensure your proxy correctly sets these headers and that the application is configured to trust the proxy. Failure to do so may result in incorrect rate limiting or the generation of invalid URLs for client pairing.

  89: 
  90: The platform does **not** inject `device_id` into the body in V1 ג€” see ֲ§7 for the full contract. Idempotency is your responsibility: dedupe by `item_id` (or a sender-generated identifier you echo back) because the platform may double-deliver under retry.
  91: 
  92: ## 3. Plugin code
  93: 
  94: `src/plugin.ts`:
  95: 
  96: ```ts
  97: import {
  98:   BasePlugin,
  99:   Capability,
 100:   DismissBehavior,
 101:   registerPlugin,
 102:   type HostPreview,
 103:   type PluginManifest,
 104: } from '@syncler/plugin-sdk';
 105: 
 106: interface MyPayload {
 107:   // hostPreview is in every payload your plugin receives ג€” the host already
 108:   // drew the inbox row from it, but render() can still use it (e.g. to repeat
 109:   // the title in the detail header).
 110:   hostPreview: HostPreview;
 111:   item_id: string;
 112:   body: string;
 113:   action_label: string;
 114: }
 115: 
 116: class MyPlugin extends BasePlugin {
 117:   static manifest: PluginManifest = {
 118:     id: 'com.example.myapp',         // your plugin_identifier
 119:     name: 'My App',
 120:     version: '1.0.0',
 121:     senderId: '<your-sender-id>',    // the UUID Syncler issued you
 122:     bundleHash: '<set by sign-bundle.ts>',
 123:     signature: '<set by sign-bundle.ts>',
 124:     declaredCapabilities: [Capability.NETWORK],  // enum, not the string literal
 125:     declaredEndpoints: ['https://your-app.example.com/api/*'],
 126:     renderer: 'script',              // or 'template' for native Compose UI
 127:     cardType: 'event',               // or 'live' for persistent cards
 128:     // template / cardKeyPath are omitted here: required only when renderer
 129:     // is 'template' / cardType is 'live'. The validator rejects them when
 130:     // they don't belong, so leave them unset for an event-mode script
 131:     // plugin like this one.
 132:     dismissBehavior: DismissBehavior.DISMISS_ALL,
 133:     minPlatformVersion: '1.0.0',
 134:   };
 135: 
 136:   // onMessage is NOT invoked in V1 inbox mode. Message arrival is surfaced by
 137:   // the host-rendered row from hostPreview. If you implement it anyway, do not
 138:   // call platform.showNotification; it rejects in V1 inbox mode.
 139: 
 140:   render(payload: MyPayload): string {
 141:     // V1 recommended pattern: button handler calls `platform.network.fetch`
 142:     // directly. The `platform.message.respond` + `onAction` round-trip is
 143:     // not part of V1 inbox mode. Post directly to your declared endpoint.
 144:     return `
 145:       <div style="font-family:sans-serif;padding:16px">
 146:         <h2>${escapeHtml(payload.hostPreview.title)}</h2>
 147:         <p>${escapeHtml(payload.body)}</p>
 148:         <button id="act" style="font-size:18px;padding:12px">${escapeHtml(payload.action_label)}</button>
 149:       </div>
 150:       <script>
 151:         const itemId = ${JSON.stringify(payload.item_id)};
 152:         document.getElementById('act').onclick = async () => {
 153:           await platform.network.fetch('https://your-app.example.com/api/action', {
 154:             method: 'POST',
 155:             headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
 156:             body: JSON.stringify({
 157:               item_id: itemId,
 158:               acted_at: new Date().toISOString(),
 159:             }),
 160:           });
 161:           document.getElementById('act').textContent = 'Sent';
 162:         };
 163:       </script>
 164:     `;
 165:   }
 166: }
 167: 
 168: // Required: self-register at bundle load. Without this call the host's
 169: // dispatcher has no plugin to dispatch into, and you'll see a "missing
 170: // registerPlugin() call?" error in the card.
 171: registerPlugin(new MyPlugin());
 172: ```
 173: 
 174: Render whatever HTML/CSS/JS suits your domain. The WebView is isolated; only `platform.*` APIs cross the boundary.
 175: 
 176: **V1 card-render bridge:**
 177: - `platform.network.fetch(url, init)` ג€” works, gated by `declaredEndpoints` glob match
 178: - `platform.showNotification`, `platform.storage`, `platform.camera`, `platform.gallery`, `platform.file`, `platform.location`, `platform.message.respond` ג€” *reject* with a clear error in V1 inbox mode. For V1 dogfood, stick to `network.fetch`.
 179: 
 180: ## 4. Build + sign the plugin
 181: 
 182: ```sh
 183: # Install the SDK
 184: cd my-plugin
 185: npm install @syncler/plugin-sdk
 186: 
 187: # Build ג€” IIFE format, NOT ESM. The host loads the bundle inside a regular
 188: # `<script>` tag, which can't parse `export` statements.
 189: npx esbuild src/plugin.ts \
 190:   --bundle \
 191:   --format=iife \
 192:   --global-name=SynclerPluginExports \
 193:   --platform=browser \
 194:   --outfile=dist/plugin.bundle.js
 195: 
 196: # Sign it (positional args, tsx is required for the TS tool):
 197: npx tsx node_modules/@syncler/plugin-sdk/tools/sign-bundle.ts \
 198:   dist/plugin.bundle.js \
 199:   ~/.syncler/keys/sender.pem \
 200:   manifest.json \
 201:   manifest.signed.json
 202: ```
 203: 
 204: The tool signs the canonical-manifest-with-bundleHash-bytes (the exact bytes the Android host verifies against ג€” see `docs/crypto-spec.md` ֲ§5). `manifest.signed.json` will contain populated `bundleHash` + `signature` fields.
 205: 
 206: Host the bundle file at a stable HTTPS URL (CDN, S3, GitHub raw). For local development, debug builds of the Android app also accept plain `http://` URLs (e.g. a Python `-m http.server` on your LAN). Release builds require HTTPS.
 207: 
 208: ## 5. Publishing the plugin (your backend, one time per version)
 209: 
 210: ```python
 410: 
 411: `reason` is optional for legacy compatibility, but senders should always supply one of:
 412: 
 413: | Reason | Use when | Host UX |
 414: |---|---|---|
 415: | `superseded` | A newer version replaces this row. | Shows a subdued "newer version available" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
 416: | `compromised` | The bundle or signing key is unsafe. | Refuses to execute the bundle and shows a security banner with the decrypted payload fallback. |
 417: | `sender_disabled` | The sender/service is intentionally disabled. | Shows a neutral "sender unavailable" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
 418: | `unspecified` | You are migrating legacy tooling and cannot classify the revoke. | Shows a generic revoked banner; avoid using this for new revokes. |
 419: 
 420: The revoke request is signed by the SDK. The `reason` value is included in the signed envelope, so an intermediary cannot strip `compromised` down to a softer classification. Re-revoking a row keeps the original `revoked_at`; a higher-severity reason can promote the row, while downgrades are ignored.
 421: 
 422: ## 6. Sending a card (your backend, per event)
 423: 
 424: ```python
 425: # After pairing ג€” see SDK README for the pairing dance.
 426: client.set_pairing(user_id="...", pairing_key=b"...32-bytes...")
 427: 
 428: result = client.send_to(
 429:     user_uuid=user_uuid,
 430:     plugin_identifier="com.example.myapp",
 431:     plugin_id="<plugin_row_id from publish_plugin>",
 432:     payload={
 433:         "hostPreview": {
 434:             "title": "Something happened",
 435:             "subtitle": "Account A",
 436:             "summary": "Brief one-sentence context.",
 437:             "searchText": ["account-a", "alert"],
 438:         },
 439:         "item_id": "abc-123",
 440:         "body": "Details for the detail view.",
 441:         "action_label": "Acknowledge",
 442:     },
 443:     min_plugin_version="1.0.0",
 444: )
 445: ```
 446: 
 447: `ttl_seconds` defaults to 7 days. The server rejects envelopes that are already expired or more than 30 days in the future.
 448: 
 449: ## 7. The action callback endpoint
 450: 
 451: `https://your-app.example.com/api/action` accepts whatever body the host POSTs when the user taps an action button. The shape depends on which renderer you chose:
 452: 
 453: **Script renderer** ג€” your `onclick` handler builds the body via `platform.network.fetch`. In the ֲ§3 example that's:
 454: 
 455: ```http
 456: POST /api/action
 457: Content-Type: application/json
 458: 
 459: { "item_id": "...", "acted_at": "..." }
 460: ```
 461: 
 462: **Template renderer** ג€” the host POSTs the **full decrypted payload** as the body, verbatim. There's no JS hook to intervene. Your endpoint receives the whole payload JSON; pull whatever fields you need server-side. No `Authorization` header is added by the host (the user's Syncler bearer token never reaches your endpoint ג€” security boundary). If you need request authentication, HMAC the payload using a sender-specific secret your backend shares out of band with itself, or rely on TLS + endpoint allowlisting alone.
 463: 
 464: Note: the platform does **not** inject `device_id` into the body for you in V1. If you need to distinguish which device acted, include a sender-generated identifier in your payload and (for script renderer) have the plugin echo it back. For template renderer, your `card_key` (or any other field in the payload) serves the same dedupe role. Dedupe by `item_id` / `card_key` alone if a single tap is what you care about.
 465: 
 466: - Status 200 -> recorded.
 467: - Status 409 -> idempotent dedupe (already saw this item); platform may retry on transient network errors so be ready.
 468: - Status 4xx other -> platform surfaces a generic failure to the plugin's promise.
 469: 
 470: ```python
 471: # Flask example ג€” dedupe by item_id alone in V1.
 472: @app.post("/api/action")
 473: def action():
 474:     data = request.json
 475:     item_id = data["item_id"]
 476:     if Action.query.filter_by(item_id=item_id).first():
 477:         return "", 409
 478:     db.session.add(Action(item_id=item_id, acted_at=data["acted_at"]))
 479:     db.session.commit()
 480:     return "", 200
 481: ```
 482: 
 483: ## 8. Testing it end-to-end
 484: 
 485: 1. Install the Syncler Android app (`./gradlew :app:installDebug`).
 486: 2. Sign up + log in. The app auto-enrolls this device with the server.
 487: 3. From your backend, run a script that registers your sender and prints a pairing QR (see SDK README).
 488: 4. Tap **Pair sender** -> **Scan QR** in the Syncler app. Confirm the fingerprint matches what your script prints.
 489: 5. After confirming, the app shows your `user_id` and a `pairing_key_hex`. Copy both and feed them into your backend's `client.set_pairing(user_id, pairing_key=bytes.fromhex(...))` so it can encrypt for you.
 490: 6. Publish your plugin (`client.publish_plugin(...)`) ג€” save the `plugin_row_id`.
 491: 7. Run `client.send_to(...)` with a test payload.
 492: 8. The server pushes an `inbox.changed` event over the SSE stream the open app is subscribed to (foreground); the phone refreshes its inbox, decrypts the message, fetches your bundle (or applies your template manifest), and shows the native row within ~1s. If the app is backgrounded, FCM wakes it and the inbox refresh happens on the next foreground.
 493: 9. Tap the row to open the plugin-rendered detail view, then tap your action button.
 494: 10. Confirm your `/api/action` endpoint received the POST.
 495: 
 496: ## 9. Common errors
 497: 
 498: - **`401 invalid envelope signature`** ג€” your sender's Ed25519 key doesn't match the one registered. Re-check `private_key_path`.
 499: - **`410 plugin missing, revoked, or not owned by sender`** ג€” `plugin_id` (the row UUID) is wrong, or you accidentally used `plugin_identifier`. The two are distinct (see ֲ§5 vs ֲ§6).
 500: - **`410 recipient has no active devices`** ג€” the user has no enrolled device (signed up but never opened the app, or revoked all devices). FCM availability is *not* required; messages are stored regardless and pulled via `/v1/messages/inbox`.
 501: - **`409 nonce already used`** ג€” your code reused a nonce somehow; SDK generates fresh nonces per `send_to`, so this means you're calling `send_to` with cached envelope bytes. Rebuild.
 502: - **`429 rate limited`** ג€” back off + retry per `Retry-After` header.
 503: - **`410 plugin missing, revoked, not live-type, or not owned by sender`** (cards upsert) ג€” the plugin row's `card_type` isn't `"live"`, or the row has a non-null `revoked_at`, or the publish row's `sender_id` doesn't match the signed envelope's sender. The error message is intentionally generic so a probing caller can't distinguish the cases (don't leak which plugin UUIDs exist).
 504: - **`410 no active pairing`** (cards upsert) ג€” the recipient user has not paired with your sender, or the pairing has been revoked. The user needs to re-scan your pairing QR.
 505: - **`400 expires_at exceeds the 48h live-card cap`** (cards upsert) ג€” your supplied `expires_at` is more than 48 hours from now. Live cards are capped server-side to prevent slot squatting. Send shorter and re-upsert to extend.
 506: - **`400 expires_at is not in the future`** (cards upsert) ג€” you sent an already-expired `expires_at`. Use a future timestamp.
 507: - **`409 sequence_number not greater than existing`** (cards upsert) ג€” the existing card has a `sequence_number` ג‰¥ what you sent. Sequence must be strictly increasing per `card_key`.
 508: - **Card shows "render failed: plugin did not install __syncler_internal_dispatch ג€” missing registerPlugin() call?"** ג€” your bundle defined the plugin class but didn't call `registerPlugin(new YourPlugin())` at module scope. See ֲ§3.
 509: - **Card shows "endpoint not declared"** ג€” your `onclick` handler is calling a URL that doesn't match any pattern in your manifest's `declaredEndpoints`. Add the URL pattern (globs allowed: `https://example.com/api/*`) and re-publish.
 510: - **`HostPreviewValidationError: hostPreview.X is N UTF-8 bytes; max is M`** ג€” caught at `client.send_to` time. Trim the offending field; see ֲ§2 for the caps. UTF-8 byte counts, not characters ג€” emoji and accented characters cost more than one byte.
 511: - **Row shows "New message from {sender}" with fallback text only** ג€” your message was sent without a `hostPreview` block, or the block was malformed (logged + ignored on the device). The detail view still loads the plugin and renders normally; only the row is generic. Add a valid `hostPreview` and re-send.
 512: 
 513: Cross-reference `docs/crypto-spec.md` for the AAD + envelope canonical byte shapes if signatures disagree.
 514: 
 515: ## 10. Versioning + history

   1: import { describe, expect, it } from 'vitest';
   2: import { Capability, DismissBehavior } from '../src/enums';

   1: # Syncler Roadmap
   2: 
   3: The Syncler platform is built and released in milestones. **V1 is what ships today**; the items below it are sequenced by platform dependencies (security primitives first, capability surface second, scaling third, UX last).
   4: 
   5: This file is the public roadmap. Internal implementation phases (Phase 0 / 1 / 2 / 3 / 4) used in the codebase and consultations track *how V1 was built*; this document tracks *what comes next*.
   6: 
   7: ## V1 ג€” Foundational milestone (shipped)
   8: 
   9: - [x] Device-bound JWTs with server-side revocation enforcement
  10: - [x] Synced pairing via the encrypted user-state blob (M7 CAS state)
  11: - [x] Server-Sent Events stream for real-time hint delivery (`inbox.changed`, `state.changed`, `dismiss`, `card.upsert`, `card.delete`)
  12: - [x] Native Material 3 template renderer (no-JS plugins via JSONPath manifest)
  13: - [x] Persistent, upsertable Live Cards with server-enforced 48h TTL + sequence-monotone updates
  14: - [x] Host-owned plugin settings sheet (sender mute, pairing revoke). Sender-side plugin-row revoke (`client.revoke_plugin(...)`) is a separate published-side API; the host UI exposes pairing revoke, not plugin-row revoke.
  15: - [x] Cross-device dismiss filter (server-side `DeliveryStatus` join)
  16: - [x] Per-device envelope auth-token isolation for template-renderer action POSTs
  17: 
  18: ## V1.5 ג€” Plugin runtime + key hygiene
  19: 
  20: 1. **Multi-process plugin host.** Move JS plugin execution to a dedicated Android process via AIDL/Binder. Isolates a crashing or runaway plugin from the host UI process and gives us a clean ProcessRecord boundary for the OS to kill independently.
  21: 2. **Native Kotlin plugin runtime (out-of-process).** A second plugin format alongside the JS bundle: a signed AAR loaded into the isolated process. Performance + platform-API parity for plugin authors who want a native experience, with the IPC boundary preventing in-process ClassLoader poisoning.
  22: 3. **Master-key rotation.** UX + protocol for rotating the user's 32-byte master key without losing access to historical state. Required before per-device encryption (#4) lands.
  23: 4. **Per-device envelope encryption.** Senders encrypt the payload separately for each of the user's enrolled devices, keyed by per-device public keys instead of the shared user master key. Enables forward secrecy and immediate per-device revocation without rotating user-wide keys.
  24: 5. **Durable nonce-replay protection.** Move the per-sender nonce registry from in-memory to Postgres so a worker restart can't accept a replayed envelope.
  25: 
  26: ## V2 ג€” Capability surface
  27: 
  28: 6. **Plugin capability expansion.** Add `camera`, `storage`, `file`, `location`, `gallery` to the bridge with per-grant prompts. Each capability lands with its own audit-log + user-visible permission dialog.
  29: 7. **`message.respond` + `showNotification`.** Promote action callbacks from a fire-and-forget POST to a request/response handshake the plugin can await. Add a `showNotification` bridge so non-inbox-mode flows (background alerts) work.
  30: 8. **Template renderer layouts.** Expand beyond `standard_card` to `compact_row`, `score_card`, and a handful of other layouts driven by data-class types. Each new layout ships with golden render tests.
  31: 9. **Script-fast runtime (Javy/QuickJS).** A lighter, non-WebView execution mode for purely logic-heavy plugins that don't need DOM. Faster cold-start and less memory than the current WebView path.
  32: 
  33: ## V3 ג€” Two-way + scaling
  34: 
  35: 10. **WebSocket two-way channel.** Bidirectional, low-latency channel between plugins and their backends; covers chat, live cursors, presence. Complements but does not replace the SSE hint channel for V1's pull-then-render model.
  36: 11. **`platform.live.subscribe(...)` for script plugins.** API for a script bundle to subscribe to a named feed and receive incremental updates without polling.
  37: 12. **Field-level live subscriptions on templates.** Update specific template fields without re-rendering the whole card ג€” the live-card path today is whole-card upsert; this adds a finer grain.
  38: 13. **Redis pub/sub for SSE scaling.** Move the in-process event bus to a shared backplane so the SSE fanout works across multiple FastAPI workers and pods.
  39: 
  40: ## V4 ג€” UX polish
  41: 
  42: 14. **Guided lost-device rotation flow.** Click-through UX for: revoke lost device ג†’ re-pair on trusted devices ג†’ rotate master key (depends on V1.5 #3). Today the user does steps 1ג€“2 by hand; this automates the sequence.
  43: 15. **Per-plugin user preferences.** Notification cadence, label overrides, delivery-window scheduling, do-not-disturb integration ג€” all surfaced from the host's settings sheet without plugin-side code.
  44: 
  45: ---
  46: 
  47: Cross-reference: implementation-level work tracked in `.triad/50-agreement-and-plan.md`. Plugin authors should read `docs/integration-guide.md` and `docs/crypto-spec.md` ג€” those two documents are the public contract.

   1: # trading-bot
   2: 
   3: Minimal Syncler sender example. Sends synthetic trading reports to a paired user every 30 minutes.
   4: 
   5: ## Setup
   6: 
   7: ```sh
   8: pip install -e ../../sdk-python
   9: python bot.py register     # one-time
  10: python bot.py pair         # writes pairing.png; scan in the Syncler app
  11: python bot.py set-pairing <user_id> <pairing_key_hex>
  12: python bot.py loop         # sends every SYNCLER_TICK_SECONDS (default 1800)
  13: ```
  14: 
  15: `state.json` is written next to `bot.py` and holds `sender_id`, `user_id`,
  16: `pairing_key_hex`, `plugin_row_id`. Delete it to reset.
  17: 
  18: ## Publishing the plugin
  19: 
  20: This example doesn't ship a plugin; it just exercises the sender side. To
  21: make incoming messages render on the phone, you'd:
  22: 
  23: 1. Write a `TradingPlugin` following the structure in `docs/integration-guide.md`,
  24:    build + sign it.
  25: 2. `client.publish_plugin(...)` to get a `plugin_row_id`.
  26: 3. Set `plugin_row_id` in `state.json`.

  44:   });
