.\docs\crypto-spec.md:276:**`user_id` is REQUIRED in the envelope.** Without it, a delete signature valid for one user's card could be replayed against another user's card with a coincidentally matching `(sender_id, card_key)` — the table is uniquely keyed on `(sender_id, user_id, card_key)`, so the lookup would otherwise be ambiguous. .\docs\integration-guide.md:36:- **Per-device dismiss (server-side filter).** When the user dismisses a message on device A, `/v1/messages/{id}/dismiss` writes a `DeliveryStatus` row keyed on `(message_id, device_id=A)`. Subsequent calls to `/v1/messages/inbox` from device A LEFT JOIN `DeliveryStatus` for `device_id=A` and filter rows where `dismissed_at IS NOT NULL` out of A's feed. The dismiss SSE event still fans out to *all* of the user's devices, but the server-side filter is per-device — devices B, C, etc. receive the hint and refresh, but their own feeds keep the row until they dismiss it themselves. V1 design: dismiss is a per-device gesture (some users want a card visible elsewhere); cross-device "dismiss everywhere" is a V1.5 add.

.\docs\integration-guide.md:498:- **`401 invalid envelope signature`** — your sender's Ed25519 key doesn't match the one registered. Re-check `private_key_path`.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:500:- **`410 recipient has no active devices`** — the user has no enrolled device (signed up but never opened the app, or revoked all devices). FCM availability is *not* required; messages are stored regardless and pulled via `/v1/messages/inbox`.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:504:- **`410 no active pairing`** (cards upsert) — the recipient user has not paired with your sender, or the pairing has been revoked. The user needs to re-scan your pairing QR.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:513:Cross-reference `docs/crypto-spec.md` for the AAD + envelope canonical byte shapes if signatures disagree.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:532:2. **Rotate keys**: For any sender that handled sensitive data, the user should **re-pair** on a trusted device. This generates a new 32-byte AES key for that sender, ensuring that any future messages from them cannot be decrypted by the lost device (even if it were to come back online).
.\docs\integration-guide.md:537:**Seven pages.** If you needed more than that to integrate, the SDK has a DX problem — file a finding back at the Syncler team.

.\docs\integration-guide.md:36:- **Per-device dismiss (server-side filter).** When the user dismisses a message on device A, `/v1/messages/{id}/dismiss` writes a `DeliveryStatus` row keyed on `(message_id, device_id=A)`. Subsequent calls to `/v1/messages/inbox` from device A LEFT JOIN `DeliveryStatus` for `device_id=A` and filter rows where `dismissed_at IS NOT NULL` out of A's feed. The dismiss SSE event still fans out to *all* of the user's devices, but the server-side filter is per-device — devices B, C, etc. receive the hint and refresh, but their own feeds keep the row until they dismiss it themselves. V1 design: dismiss is a per-device gesture (some users want a card visible elsewhere); cross-device "dismiss everywhere" is a V1.5 add.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:74:`searchText` is folded into the host's inbox search alongside title, subtitle, summary, and sender name. **Triad Result: GREEN With Two Pushbacks**

Both reviewers validate the external DX critique as materially correct. The proposed Phase 4.1 split is mostly right, but I would adjust two points:

1. **#1 should be stricter than proposed:** make `bundleHash` exactly **64 hex chars** and `signature` exactly **128 hex chars**. The repo is SHA-256 + Ed25519 today; accepting 128-char bundle hashes implies SHA-512 support the rest of the stack does not advertise.

2. **#4 should not be deferred wholesale:** a minimal plugin already exists at `sdk-plugin/examples/minimal`, but it is undiscoverable from `examples/`, still uses `"00"` placeholders, and is not a real round-trip example. Phase 4.1 should clean and advertise the existing minimal example; a full `examples/minimal-plugin/` or scaffold command is Phase 4.5, not V1.5+.

**Per-Finding Decision**

| Finding | Validate | Classify | Prescription |
|---|---|---|---|
| #1 bundleHash/signature footgun | Correct. `sdk-plugin/src/manifest.ts:126-130` only checks hex; README/example use `"00"` at `sdk-plugin/README.md:34-35`, `sdk-plugin/examples/minimal/src/plugin.ts:9-10`, `manifest.json:6-7`. Server expects 32-byte bundle hash + 64-byte sig at `server/app/schemas.py:511-544`. | **Phase 4.1** | Validator: `bundleHash` exactly 64 hex, `signature` exactly 128 hex. Update tests. Replace/annotate `"00"` placeholders as unsigned-dev only or `<filled by sign-bundle.ts>`. |
| #2 pairing half-built | Correct. Python README has TODO-ish M7 wording at `sdk-python/README.md:29-37`; guide uses manual copy at `docs/integration-guide.md:483-490`; Android explicitly says dev-mode handoff at `PairingScreen.kt:255-263`. | **Phase 4.1 docs + V1.5 automation** | Phase 4.1: remove “M7 wires this” language and make §8 the canonical V1 manual pairing flow. V1.5: automated bootstrap/polling flow. |
| #3 wildcard rule buried | Correct. Guide shows globs but not single-segment behavior at `docs/integration-guide.md:125`, `:177`, `:509`. TS implements single segment at `sdk-plugin/src/network.ts:48-61`; Android too. | **Phase 4.1** | Add paragraph near `declaredEndpoints`: `*` matches one host segment or one path segment only; `/api/*` does not match `/api/a/b`; `https://*.example.com` does not match `a.b.example.com`. |
| #4 no example plugin | Partially correct. Root `examples/` only has `trading-bot`, which says no plugin at `examples/trading-bot/README.md:18-26`; but `sdk-plugin/examples/minimal` exists. | **Phase 4.1 small cleanup + Phase 4.5 full example** | Phase 4.1: make existing minimal example discoverable, remove misleading placeholders/capability mismatch. Phase 4.5: real round-trip plugin/backend/scaffold. |
| #5 fetch contract undocumented | Correct. Guide only says it works at `docs/integration-guide.md:176-178`. Contract lives in `sdk-plugin/src/network.ts`, `sdk-plugin/src/platform.ts`, `PluginBridge.kt`, `NetworkBridge.kt`. | **Phase 4.1** | Add “Network fetch contract” under §3: HTTP 4xx/5xx resolve as `Response`; endpoint/capability/cleartext/offline/timeout reject; timeout is 30s; release requires HTTPS. |
| #6 roadmap ignores DX | Correct. `docs/ROADMAP.md:18-43` is platform/runtime-focused and has no DX track. | **Phase 4.1** | Add Developer Experience subsection listing automated pairing, full example plugin, scaffold, and docs/validator polish status. |
| Structural pitfalls/errors | Correct. §9 mixes server errors and client pitfalls at `docs/integration-guide.md:496-512`. | **Phase 4.1** | Rename §9 to “Common server errors”; add “Common pitfalls”: unsigned placeholders, single-segment wildcard, missing `registerPlugin`, `card_key` vs `cardKeyPath`, template/script mismatches. |

**Cross-Finding Interactions**

#1 and #4 should land together enough that the minimal example no longer teaches the `"00"` pattern. #3 and #5 should land together because endpoint allowlisting is part of the fetch contract. #2 and #6 should land together so pairing is honestly documented now and tracked as future DX automation.

**Overall**

Ready to execute Phase 4.1. No blocker.

Scope I’d execute now: #1 validator/tests/docs, #2 wording cleanup, #3 wildcard docs, #5 fetch contract docs, structural §9 split, #6 roadmap DX track, plus minimal-example discoverability cleanup for #4. Full runnable example/scaffold should be Phase 4.5 before broader rollout.
